## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE-based growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P and possibly explicit time forcing t. This matches classical ecological population-dynamics models formulated as differential equations with density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting, and environmental/seasonal time variation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant inflow/outflow added to proportional growth)
- Linear density dependence (generalized self-limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth proportional to P^2)
- Logistic growth ODE (carrying capacity via quadratic term): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (K encoded as c1 = 1/K)
- Theta-logistic (flexible density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (controls how sharply growth declines with P)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines with log of size)
- Richards / generalized logistic (extra shape parameter): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)**c2 (changes approach-to-capacity curvature)
- Allee effect (bistability at low density): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (P - c2) (negative growth below threshold P=c2)
- Power-law growth (allometric or autocatalytic): dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (superlinear c1>1 can yield rapid acceleration; sublinear c1<1 slows)
- Saturating per-capita growth via rational form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) / (1 + c2 * P) (crowding with gradual saturation of density effect)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environmental modulation of per-capita rate)
- Time-varying (trend) growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P or dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (slow drift or exponential change in environment)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Use per-capita growth g(P,t) = dP_dt / P: if g is ~constant, expect dP_dt ∝ P; if g decreases ~linearly with P, expect logistic-type dP_dt = c0*P - c1*P^2.
- Equilibria correspond to roots of dP_dt(P,t): multiple real roots in P suggest Allee-type (three equilibria: extinction, unstable threshold, positive stable).
- Carrying capacity behavior: if dP_dt crosses zero near a stable positive P* and becomes negative above it, include a factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - c*P^k).
- If growth slows strongly only at large P (more gradual than quadratic), consider Gompertz (log term) or rational damping /(1 + c*P).
- If early-time growth appears “too fast” compared with exponential (accelerating per-capita rate), consider superlinear dP_dt ∝ P^c with c>1 (autocatalytic/aggregation effects).
- If dP_dt at P≈0 is negative or near-zero despite positive growth at moderate P, include an Allee threshold factor (P - c).
- If residuals versus t are periodic after accounting for P-dependence, include sinusoidal forcing in t multiplying P (seasonal fecundity/survival).
- If inferred parameters vary systematically with t (e.g., trend), model rate parameters as c0 + c1*t or c0*exp(c1*t) multiplying P rather than adding high-degree polynomials in P.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG7)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P**c9
Candidate formulas: 62

GT depends only on **P** (no **t**) and is a sum of three terms:
- a cubic-in-P polynomial part coming from  
  \(0.7213(-1+P/6.6511)(1-P/13.5381)P + 0.7213(1-P/13.5381)P\),
- plus \(0.7213\,P^{1/3}\).

Expand the polynomial part:
\[
(-1+P/a)(1-P/b)P = \left(-1 + P(\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b) - \tfrac{P^2}{ab}\right)P
= -P + (\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b)P^2 - \tfrac{1}{ab}P^3
\]
and
\[
(1-P/b)P = P - \tfrac{1}{b}P^2.
\]
Adding these cancels the linear term, leaving
\[
\text{GT} = 0.7213\left[\left(\tfrac1a+\tfrac1b-\tfrac1b\right)P^2 - \tfrac{1}{ab}P^3\right] + 0.7213 P^{1/3}
= 0.7213\left[\tfrac{1}{a}P^2 - \tfrac{1}{ab}P^3\right] + 0.7213 P^{1/3},
\]
with \(a=6.6511\), \(b=13.5381\). So GT is exactly of the form
\[
\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P^2 + \gamma P^3
\]
with **no** \(P\) term, no constant term, and no \(t\)-dependence.

Therefore, any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to exactly \(\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P^2 + \gamma P^3\), with no extra functional dependence (sin/exp/log/rational in \(P\) or any \(t\) dependence) and no extra powers.

Now check candidates:

1. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)\).  
   Set \(c4=0\) to remove \(t\). Combine \(P^2\) terms: \((c2+c3)P^2\). Matches the required form. **Can match.**

2. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3\sin(c4 t + c5)\).  
   Set \(c3=0\). Remaining is correct form. **Can match.**

3. Same as (2) but has extra \(+P^2\).  
   That just fixes part of the \(P^2\) coefficient; choose \(c2\) accordingly, set sine coefficient \(c3=0\). **Can match.**

4. Has \(+P^2\) and \(+c3\exp(P c4)\).  
   Exponential in \(P\) must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\) remains. **Can match.**

5. Like (4) without the explicit \(+P^2\): still can set \(c3=0\). **Can match.**

6. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c4\exp(P c5)\).  
   Set \(c4=0\). Combine \(P^2\). **Can match.**

7–9. Include \(\sin(\text{function of }P)\).  
   Set the sine coefficient to 0 (c3 or c4 or c3). Remaining is correct polynomial form. **Can match (all 7,8,9).**

10. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c5 P^{c4}\).  
   Need no extra power beyond \(1/3,2,3\). Set \(c5=0\) to remove \(P^{c4}\). Then OK. **Can match.**

11. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c4 P^{c3}\).  
   Set \(c4=0\). Then OK. **Can match.**

12. Same as (11) plus \(+P^2\). Adjust \(c2\), set \(c4=0\). **Can match.**

13–16. Include rational terms like \(\frac{P c3}{P c4+c5}+\frac{c6}{P c4+c5}\).  
   These are not polynomial in \(P\) unless forced to vanish. Set the numerators to 0 (e.g., \(c3=0,c6=0\); similarly for 14–16). Then remaining terms are \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\) (and in 16 also \(P^{c5}c6\) which can be removed by setting that coefficient \(c6=0\)). **Can match (13–16).**

17. Has extra linear terms \(P*c3 + P*c4\) and a log term.  
   Set \(c3=0,c4=0\) to remove linear; set \(c7=0\) to remove log; set \(c6=0\) to remove \(P^{c5}c6\). Left with \(P^3,P^2\) (and can add \(P^{1/3}\)? actually 17 has no \(P^{1/3}\) term, so it cannot produce \(P^{1/3}\) unless \(P^{c5}\) is used with \(c5=1/3\). But \(P^{c5}c6\) was set to 0 above; instead, keep it and set \(c5=1/3\) and \(c6=0.7213\) (or appropriate), while still zeroing other unwanted terms. Then it can supply the \(P^{1/3}\) term. So: choose \(c5=1/3\), \(c6=\alpha\), \(c0=\gamma\), \(c1=\beta\), \(c2=0\) (or vice versa), and set \(c3=c4=c7=0\). **Can match.**

18. \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2 + P^{c3}c4 + c5\sin(P c6 + c7)\).  
   Need no linear term: set \(c2=0\). Remove sine: \(c5=0\). Use \(P^{c3}c4\) to create \(P^{1/3}\): set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=\alpha\). Then choose \(c0,c1\) for cubic/quadratic. **Can match.**

19. Similar to 18 but also has an explicit \(P*c3\). Set \(c2=0,c3=0\), sine coefficient \(c6=0\). Use \(P^{c4}c5\) with \(c4=1/3\). **Can match.**

20. Has linear terms \(P*c3 + P*c4\) and sine. Set \(c3=c4=0\), sine coefficient \(c7=0\). Use \(P^{c5}c6\) with \(c5=1/3\). **Can match.**

21. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + c3 P^2 + c4 P + c5\).  
   GT has no \(P\) or constant: set \(c4=0,c5=0\). Combine \(P^2\). **Can match.**

22. Has \(+P^2\), \(+P*c3\), \(+c4\). Set \(c3=0,c4=0\), adjust \(c2\). **Can match.**

23. Has \(+P*c3 + c4\). Set both 0. **Can match.**

24. \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P c2 + P^{c3}c4 + c5\).  
   Set \(c2=0,c5=0\), set \(c3=1/3\) and \(c4=\alpha\). **Can match.**

25. Has log term in \(P\). Set its coefficient \(c3=0\). Then OK (with the extra \(+P^2\) absorbed into \(c2\)). **Can match.**

26. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^3 + c2 P^2 + P*c3\).  
   Set \(c3=0\). **Can match.**

27–28. Have log term in \(P\). Set log coefficient to 0. **Can match.**

29. \(P^3 c0 + P^2 c1 + P^2 c2 + P c3 + P c4 + P^{c5}c6\).  
   Remove linear: set \(c3=c4=0\). Use \(P^{c5}c6\) with \(c5=1/3\) for the fractional power. Quadratic coefficient is \(c1+c2\). **Can match.**

30–32. Include \(t\)-dependent factor \((c4+t)^{c5}\) multiplied by \(P\) (or \(P*c4*(...)^{...}\)).  
   GT has no \(t\) and no linear-in-\(P\) term. The only way is to kill these terms by setting their coefficients to 0 (the multiplier of the whole \(P*(...)^{...}\) term). In 30 that is \(c3\); in 31 that is \(c4\); in 32 that is \(c3\). Set to 0, leaving polynomial + \(P^{1/3}\). **Can match (30–32).**

33–38. Pure combinations of \(P^{1/3},P^3,P^2\) plus possibly constants or extra \(P^2\) factor.  
   Any constant must be 0 (33–35). Candidate 36 includes an extra fixed \(+P^2\) which can be absorbed by choosing \(c2\). Candidate 37 already matches the form. Candidate 38 matches. **Can match (33–38) with constants set appropriately (and constant terms set to 0).**

39–50. Contain various \(t\)-dependent rational terms and/or \(t\) linear terms.  
   Since GT has no \(t\), all such terms must be eliminated by setting their coefficients to 0 (e.g., the numerators’ coefficients or the whole added term’s coefficient). Each of these candidates has free coefficients multiplying the \(t\)-dependent parts, so they can be set to 0, leaving the needed \(P^{1/3},P^2,P^3\) structure. **Can match (39–50).**

51–53. Include \(\exp(c4 t)\) terms.  
   Set the exponential coefficient to 0 (c3 or c4). Then OK. **Can match.**

54–56. Include \(t*(P+c4)^{c5}\) terms.  
   Set the coefficient multiplying the whole \(t*(...)^{...}\) term to 0 (c3 or c4). Then OK. **Can match.**

57–59. Include \(\log(c4 t+1)\) terms.  
   Set log coefficient to 0 (c3 or c4). Then OK. **Can match.**

60–62. Include \(t^{c4}\) terms.  
   Set the coefficient of the \(t^{...}\) term to 0 (c3 or c4). Then OK. **Can match.**

Since many candidates can be reduced to exactly \(\alpha P^{1/3}+\beta P^2+\gamma P^3\) by zeroing extraneous terms and choosing coefficients appropriately, at least one match exists.

I need to first simplify the Ground Truth expression to understand what functional form it takes.

## Ground Truth Simplification

GT: `0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333`

Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511035054181695`, `d = 13.538092585698905`.

**First term:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= `a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P`

**Second term:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P`

**Third term:** `a*P^(1/3)`

Let me combine the first two terms. Factor out `a*(1 - P/d)*P`:
= `a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(-1 + P/b) + 1] + a*P^(1/3)`
= `a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b) + a*P^(1/3)`
= `a*(P²/b)*(1 - P/d) + a*P^(1/3)`
= `a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d) + a*P^(1/3)`

So GT = `a*P^(1/3) + (a/b)*P² - (a/(b*d))*P³`

Computing coefficients:
- P^(1/3): `a = 0.72136`
- P²: `a/b = 0.72136/6.6511 ≈ 0.10845`
- P³: `-a/(b*d) = -0.72136/(6.6511*13.5381) ≈ -0.008012`

**GT = c₀*P^(1/3) + c₁*P³ + c₂*P²**

where c₀ ≈ 0.72136, c₁ ≈ -0.008012, c₂ ≈ 0.10845.

This is simply: **P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2**

Now I need to check which candidates can reduce to exactly this form (no dependence on `t`, no extra basis functions that can't be zeroed).

  - Similarly for 3,34,36,38 variants with extra P² that can be absorbed.
